### Post by MichealH on 2010-01-30
Lets See what we Will come Out with here! Hope you've been brewing up these Desktops!

Please read the Rules **BEFORE** Posting:

> Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc. If you are Quoting It make sure you remove the IMG Tags and replace the link with something (e.g "*snip*").

3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed. If you want to post something Offtopic Do it somewhere Else!

4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone. This is Not the place to be posting shots like that If you are going to Make sure It is a **LINK** and not a IMG and with "NSFW" beside it.

5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

**Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why. There is [B]NO** Excuse for non-Resized Thumbnails I use Imageshack to resize Its only 2 minutes more and It never hurt nobody. If I can take the time so can you![/B]

**_Following these Simple Rules will ensure you don't get a firm warning off the administrators. Please If you don't read these rules or don't obey by them please don't post! You would only cause trouble._**

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-01-31
> **matty-guy said:**
> 

Openbox as window manager using my own theme. GTK theme is shiki-wise modified a bit. My own tint2 theme too, based off one that I forget. Any other information, just ask. Can people also give me feedback, I really want to know what people want me to change.
The most important thing is whether it works for you or not?.... Don't change something just because people want you to.

Personally, I don't have a problem with all the grey, but think the primary tone of your GTK is a bit too close to the dominant colour in your wallpaper, or maybe the second most dominant (I assume you made the wall as well?). Things tend to look weird if the theme and wallpaper are too close in value. (Although I'm guilty of this as well when it comes to my black setups)

Tint2 looks good, though.

This is highly subjective, but those large squares/boxes next to the menu headers in you OBmenu make if feel rather bulky to me... you could try making them a bit smaller, perhaps?

Just offering my 2 cents since you asked... I don't mean any disrespect.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-01-31
> **MichealH said:**
> I have always wanted to know how you do that desktop file menu could you please give me a Link? Thanks

```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:globalmenu-team/ppa
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install gnome-globalmenu
```

Then add it as an applet to your panel.

---

### Post by Amtal on 2010-01-31
Mostly the same as the last shot I posted. Fonts are different. Ended up being lazy and going with Lucida Grande for almost everything. Using Lucida Mac Bold for window titles. The clock is [Geosans Light]("http://www.dafont.com/geo-sans-light.font").

Widget Style: [QtCurve from here]("http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/retroactive-150774364")
Windows: [Aurorae using AirGlass-White]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Airglass-white++%5BAURORAE%5D?content=108392")
Icons: [Kycons]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Kycons?content=115097")
Font: Lucida Grande
Console [Font: Envy Code R]("http://damieng.com/blog/2008/05/26/envy-code-r-preview-7-coding-font-released")
Plasma: [Glassified]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Glassified?content=81388")
Apps: Konsole, SMPlayer, Dolphin, Pidgin

[URL="http://dl.dropbox.com/u/116194/Screenshots/alpha_2010-01-31__22%3A26%3A33.jpeg"][IMG]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/116194/Screenshots/thumbnails/alpha_2010-01-31__22%3A26%3A33-thumb.jpeg[/IMG]

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-02-01
Here's mine...

Using a modified version of shiki-colors (brave). My own emerald window borders. Compiz desk menu and gnome-do docky. I used to use global applet menus in the top bar, but the lack of firefox and openoffice support irritated me so I switched to using the window title applet. Used a compiz trick to remove window decorations for maximised windows so that they blend into the top bar. Windows can be maximised by the windows button applet or from the gnome menu in the top right corner.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-01
> **el_itur said:**
> Can you hand me the details? specially the wallpaper, it's lovely
The wallpaper is from somewhere in deviantart, but I can't remember the author, and there are too many wallpapers named "rainbow" something.
[Here's a link]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/Rainbow-2.jpg") though.
The GTK and Metacity themes are elementary, the icon theme is AnyColourYouLike with the sunken effect and black colour (you'll see what I mean after you get them), and they're all available at gnome-look.org.

The top bar is gnome-panel, with globalmenu (for whick I gave instructions earlier in the thread :P), the music applet for the music controls, and the clock. I've used a custom panel background which I have attached below. I had to edit the theme's gtkrc file to get it to show transparent for everything though.

Bottom is AWN with custom theme.

That's about it isn't it?

### Post by Islington on 2010-02-01
Trying a dose of simplicity. There is one small panel that has a clock, and the system tray on autohide, it only pops up when it has something to tell me.

Firefox navigation is done through krunner, as are google and other searches. Krunner also does most of my launching/searching.
Window management is done exclusively through "Present Windows" which is binded to a screen corner or keyboard shortcuts. The default desktop is a folderview showing my desktop folder, some widgets I use are put on the dashboard which is binded to another corner, expo and 'show desktop' are corner bound. I wish I could explain more, but this is the best setup I have done so far on my laptop. oh wallpaper is something chopped up from flickr.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-02-01
> **matty-guy said:**
> I'm not sure what window tiling is, but if you're referring to the window placements and sizes, then just click and drag to change the window size, and drag to somewhere on the screen is how I do it.
As well as the links gutterslob posted, you might want to check out an application in the repos called wmctrl. I found it to be a godsend, after doing what you described for years. I rarely manually resize or move a window anymore.

[url=http://img716.imageshack.us/img716/9736/wmctrl.jpg][img]http://img716.imageshack.us/img716/2364/wmctrlsmall.jpg[/img]
http://img716.imageshack.us/img716/9736/wmctrl.jpg[/url]

And if you can't visualise the keyboard shortcuts:

Shift+Alt+* moves windows.
Ctrl+Alt+* resizes windows.

Horizontal movement/resizing occurs with the keys QWER and ASDF.
Vertical with ZXCV.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-02-02
I'd always wondered what tiling utilities existed for OSX.

Oh and I forgot to mention: when figuring out your -e argument values, x/y placement values take into consideration you window decorations, while w/h size values don't. 

So, if you're figuring out your placement values and you've got a horizontal resolution of 1024, your horizontal placement values should be 0, 256, 512 and 768.

However, if you're figuring out your window width values, to avoid overlapping, you've got to subtract the width of the window decoration. If the decoration is 3 pixel wide on each side, you've got to subtract 6 pixels from the values used previously, giving you horizontal window sizes of 250, 506 and 762.

You've got to use the same process for vertical placement and size values.

---

### Post by h!v on 2010-02-02
> **MacJack said:**
> :D Is that an image previewer in the first shot, and if so how does it work (controls)?
It's not only image previewer. That's Gloobus-preview and it supports other files (txt, movie, sound etc). You need patched Nautilus(provided by ppa) so when you select file and hit spacebar it activates. Arrows are used to navigate through files.

### Post by narf41 on 2010-02-02

### Post by eightmillion on 2010-02-03
> **sideaway said:**
> Mate I love this, can I ***please*** have more information? I feel something for my (new!!!) laptop coming up perhaps. I'm getting that linux itch again!

Sorry for the delay. It's KDE 4.4 using the search and launch containment for the desktop. The wallpaper is [this]("http://crimson-designs.deviantart.com/art/Bruised-Red-Wood-11647331") tiled. The icons are iKon. There's a link to them in lzfy's signature. The window decorations are Bespin with the netbook orientation option enabled and the widget them is also Bespin. The terminal is Konsole with window decorations, menus and scroll bars disabled. The plasma theme is Oxygen. The fonts are Segoe Semibold and Inconsolata for the terminal. And finally, the clock in the corner is [this Superkaramba widget]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/3D+Desktop+Clock?content=95681").

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-04
> **Mykle87 said:**
> I really dig your desktop gutterslob. Would you mind sharing on insight on your setup? I having some trouble putting together a clean Openbox desktop. I decided to use the alternate command-line only install which I think is holding me way back. Which version of linux are you running? Are you running only Openbox or are you running it on top of Gnome or KDE or something?[QUOTE=sideaway;8771900]He could be using Crunchbang linux, a Openbox version on an Ubuntu base, Corenomial has done well

[http://crunchbanglinux.org/](http://crunchbanglinux.org/)[/QUOTE]

Mine's actually a minimal Debian (Sid) + Openbox standalone install, but it immitates CrunchBang heavily (since it's what I used before this).... as Sideway said, Corenominal (Phillip) got it so damn right. You could try it out or at least check out their forums for some ideas.

It's actually a pretty straightforwats setup Mykle87... this "clenliness" you speak of might be because I tend to use as few colours as possible in my setups (most of my screenshots are monochrome-ish, if you backtrack), which may or may not be your cup of tea.

As for what I use, it's basically Conky for the system monitor on the top left, and tint2 for my panel.  I tend to avoid icons as much as possible, since I prefer typography.... and all that lua-conky crap is a big no-no for me as well. The tint2 is configured to show only text instead of icons for the tasks. The icons you see on the tint2 systray (bottom right) are from the Black-Gnome iconset (available at gnome-look), but I made my own volwheel icon and changed the colour of the default bluetooth icon. All my wallpapers are self-made, which may contribute to the overall clean/minimalist look you see.

I've included 2 links ... first one contains my tint2, conky and terminator (terminal) configs, plus all the .ttf fonts I use in that screenshot (just in case you don't have them already), while the second one contains the same configs plus a few wallpapers I made (they may aid you in getting an idea of what you might want to use as wallpaper in future), which you can flip horizontally if you prefer your conky on the right.

[http://www.mediafire.com/?mnj0uzndnnw](http://www.mediafire.com/?mnj0uzndnnw)
[http://www.mediafire.com/?nmyl3ayhw3y](http://www.mediafire.com/?nmyl3ayhw3y)

Hope this helps... sorry about the text-wall.
Feel free to ask if you need anything else.

Cheers.

Edit:
@ethanol and chuckles
Like I said, anime/manga (and people in general) isn't my forte... I'll take the Bjork reference as a complement, though :P

### Post by sertse on 2010-02-04
The rule are guidelines, and some of the people here are running exceeding complicated setups that are getting harder to "just show details". Especially the ones who make/tweak their own themes/conkies/scripts. 

Still, others of us here post so often that there is little difference from shot to shot, and therefore a bit bothersome to post details again and again.  

Then there's the argument that asking for details is at least some incentive for people to get feedback/praise on shots, which half of us are just kids craving for  validation. :P

Atm: I'm still trying to make my pokemon wallpaper, (posted a couple of pages back) work, - I've slapped "Elegant Cold Blue" (and here I wonder, do I need to search where I found that? It's a quick google search will show it quickly if people are interested) for now, it's passable, but not really fitting. Icons are GartoonRedux (prob one of the most unique styles, most downloaded iconsets around).

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-02-04
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Hi everyone...I hope you don't mind a little self-publicising post :oops:

I have finally set up my PPA on Launchpad, so there are a couple packages up there if you're interested...I've put up the (very much work in progress) Token Dark icon theme I'm working on, and my Conky Widgets script (with all the widgets I've written so far). If you install them, you'll get updates as I push them.

Anyway, the addy is in the screenie, and my sig :)

Wallpaper is "The Source" by imrik, on DeviantArt, icons are my (work in progress) Token Dark theme, GTK is my own Venus theme, and Metacity is Aurora. <-- Hey look! Details!
[ATTACH]146002[/ATTACH][ATTACH]146003[/ATTACH]

Amazing icon set!

But there are some broken symlinks... at least in the tar.gz file I downloaded from the PPA. An absolute path to your home folder is hardcoded in some symlinks, like this:
```
~/.icons/Token Dark/128x128/places% ls -l xfce-trash_empty.png
lrwxrwxrwx 1 danielrmt danielrmt 60 Fev  4 20:31 xfce-trash_empty.png -> **/home/alison/.icons/Token Dark/128x128/places/**user-trash.png
```
to fix this I'd have to run
```
ln -sf user-trash.png xfce-trash_empty.png
```
and the ls -l output would be relative:
```
~/.icons/Token Dark/128x128/places% ls -l xfce-trash_empty.png
lrwxrwxrwx 1 danielrmt danielrmt 60 Fev  4 20:31 xfce-trash_empty.png -> user-trash.png
```
I have writed a small script to fix some of those symlinks: [http://pastebin.ubuntu.com/369172/](http://pastebin.ubuntu.com/369172/)

---

### Post by MacJack on 2010-02-04
:D In KDE 4 do you know how to have the buttons on the left side of window decorations in kwin or Bespin as I downloaded a couple of themes that in the preview showed them on the left side but when installed are on the right :confused: atm spending lots of time testing themes on KDE4 with lots of inspiration from this and previous desktop threads.





Mac Snow Leopard with mostly Eikon icons.

[[IMG]http://pici.se/pictures/JLfUzCbqZ.png[/IMG]]("http://pici.se/p/large/kRfemlsVf/?size=fullsize")

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-04
> **MacJack said:**
> :D In KDE 4 do you know how to have the buttons on the left side of window decorations in kwin or Bespin as I downloaded a couple of themes that in the preview showed them on the left side but when installed are on the right :confused: 

System Preferences -> Appearance -> Windows

And there is somewhere a tab that shows you all the available things to add or remove to the window decoration. Drag them to rearrange them.

---

### Post by MacJack on 2010-02-04
> **koleoptero said:**
> System Preferences -> Appearance -> Windows

And there is somewhere a tab that shows you all the available things to add or remove to the window decoration. Drag them to rearrange them.


Thanks for the fast reply. ;)

### Post by Whistling Nixie on 2010-02-05
[IMG]http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2766/4337846946_a808689ff9.jpg[/IMG]

THEME
[Black-Diamond]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Black-Diamond?content=94653%22%20rel=%22nofollow%22%3Egnome-look.org/content/show.php/Black-Diamond?content=94653")

### Post by arzali on 2010-02-05
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> No, that's not what I'm referring to.


Notice the plain, empty space right of the pathbars? With that elementary mod theme/hack, it's not empty. Usually, no visible widget is drawn to that area unless you've dug down into the filesystem a bit.

the theme uses a toolbar background image where the pathbar is drawn on it. the buttons are almost transparent with arrows on the end. 
i think it works only with elementary nautilus because the pathbar is integrated into the toolbar.
[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/41134/bildschirmfoto_2_52xr43.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/41134/bildschirmfoto_2_52xr43.png)

### Post by sideaway on 2010-02-06
> **eightmillion said:**
> Sorry for the delay. It's KDE 4.4 using the search and launch containment for the desktop. The wallpaper is [this]("http://crimson-designs.deviantart.com/art/Bruised-Red-Wood-11647331") tiled. The icons are iKon. There's a link to them in lzfy's signature. The window decorations are Bespin with the netbook orientation option enabled and the widget them is also Bespin. The terminal is Konsole with window decorations, menus and scroll bars disabled. The plasma theme is Oxygen. The fonts are Segoe Semibold and Inconsolata for the terminal. And finally, the clock in the corner is [this Superkaramba widget]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/3D+Desktop+Clock?content=95681").
[URL="http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1399624"]
I've been trying to get the Search and Launch containment going[/URL] but I can't. Running KDE 4.4 RC3. any ideas?

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-06
@koleoptero
Thanks... It's actually an inverted and slightly simplified version of one of my art prints... the original is way better, but too bright for a desktop wallpaper.

@matty-guy
I'm honestly stumped, man.... never seen that before.... it's not exactly a white line, but more like the top and left of the windec is embossed outward... sort of like a reverse effect of drop-shadow compositing (does it happen with xcompmgr enabled, perchance?)

You say it happens with all OBT's, so I guess that can rule out having one of us take a look at your theme.

open up obconf and go to the "Appearance" tab .... is that box next to "Button order" completely blank?... if it is, just enter something like DIMC and then see if the windecs are still like that....Also, try changing the font size of the "Active window title" and "Inactive window title" to a different size.

Not sure if it'll help, but it's the only thing I can think of right now.
Sorry.

### Post by MacJack on 2010-02-07
> **suprman2020 said:**
> [[IMG]http://img69.imageshack.us/img69/3249/screenshot1xl.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img69.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot1xl.png")
[[IMG]http://img716.imageshack.us/img716/2929/screenshot2i.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img716.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot2i.png")


I'm using a combo of elementary and shiki-colors. The iconset is Meliae SVG. Does anybody know how I can get a dark panel with the elementary theme?


In your home menu and enable hidden files from the drop down menu in view tab in the toolbar, go into themes/ and into elementary folder and search panel folder.

But then if you change to a dark panel all the text will vanish so that is changed in the gtkrc file again in the elementary folder.

ok, a noob question, since I can't find an answer on google: how do I install a qt theme?

import it.

system settings>style> widget style> configure button> options> import.

### Post by 6205 on 2010-02-08
Here is my Ubuntu Karmic February 2010 desktop >>>
[http://img718.imageshack.us/img718/9732/mydesk2010.png](http://img718.imageshack.us/img718/9732/mydesk2010.png)



- Wallpaper is "Motion Wood"
[http://neodesktop.deviantart.com/art/MotionWood-Wallpapers-133685690](http://neodesktop.deviantart.com/art/MotionWood-Wallpapers-133685690)

- Special version "Nautilus Elementary" file manager
[https://launchpad.net/~am-monkeyd/+archive/nautilus-elementary-ppa](https://launchpad.net/~am-monkeyd/+archive/nautilus-elementary-ppa)

- Dock is "Docky" from PPA repository
[https://launchpad.net/~docky-core/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~docky-core/+archive/ppa)

- Icon theme "Humanity" - latest revision from Elementary Art PPA
[https://launchpad.net/~elementaryart/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~elementaryart/+archive/ppa)

- GTK theme "Humanity"
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1168984](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1168984)

- Metacity theme "Ubuntu Sun Day"
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Artwork/Incoming/Lucid/UbuntuSun](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Artwork/Incoming/Lucid/UbuntuSun)

- Fonts are Droid Sans 10

- Custom panel background image (very tiny in top left corner)
[http://img62.imageshack.us/img62/7179/panelsmall.png](http://img62.imageshack.us/img62/7179/panelsmall.png)

---

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-02-08
> **walkerk said:**
> Ok. I've editted the Litestyle OB theme to my liking...
*snip*

Looks great. 

For anyone who was interested in my openbox border problem, it would've helped if I posted it, cos it turns out it was a problem with the file. I should have tested with more than 5 themes I guess, cos by some strange chance, they all had the windows set to parentrelative, as opposed to solid, which is where my problem began. Maybe one of you guys know, but parentrelative added a hairline to the left and top, but as soon as I fiddled around with the settings I saw where I'd gone wrong.

---

### Post by walkerk on 2010-02-08
> **matty-guy said:**
> Looks great. 

For anyone who was interested in my openbox border problem, it would've helped if I posted it, cos it turns out it was a problem with the file. I should have tested with more than 5 themes I guess, cos by some strange chance, they all had the windows set to parentrelative, as opposed to solid, which is where my problem began. Maybe one of you guys know, but parentrelative added a hairline to the left and top, but as soon as I fiddled around with the settings I saw where I'd gone wrong.

I had to give the wiki a read...

[http://openbox.org/wiki/Help:Theme](http://openbox.org/wiki/Help:Theme)

OB can be a bit annoying to theme...

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-09
> **scouser73 said:**
> I like this, it's really smart.
Thank you :)
> **Mark76 said:**
> Yeah. It doesn't work properly with the Rox panels

[ATTACH]146544[/ATTACH]

See!
sudo gedit /usr/share/themes/Shiki-Brave/gtk-2.0/panel.rc

add a # at the start of the bg_pixmap[NORMAL] line and get rid of the backgrounds.

OR you can create a larger background and edit that line to use it.

I'm not really a Gnome guy, but....
It's the little things, Dave;
Try making that wretched Lua thing a bit smaller so that it's the same size as your time font (if you insist on keeping it, that is),and then ${voffset} the time so that the spacing is a bit more consistent with the other lines of info......Merge your conky's into one.... Single gnome panel would work better with your setup, I think.... terminal doesn't really need a scroolbar.... that recycle bin icon looks a bit naff (get recs from koleoptero, myusername, Giant Speck..etc for a cleaner iconset...and try to sort out that Pidgin tray icon as well)

Doesn't the Gnome panel come with an option to hide tray icons (like that arrow thingie in Xfce) ??

You know I'm not really a fan of icons on the desktop, but I understand why you might want them there (convenience)

It's just my 2 cents, Dave.... like I said, the little things.... everything else looks good and usable, though

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-11
> **kyle99 said:**
> What are you using on this?
Are you asking about the fonts used (in reference to my question) or the entire setup in general?

Anyways, here's all that's in that screenshot;
Distro = Debian Sid , WM = Openbox , Panel = tint2 , System Monitor = Conky.
Terminals (terminator) are set to transparent. The music player you see is Cplay.
System, panel and Conky fonts = Radio Space , Console fonts = Terminus.
Systray icons (bottom right) = Black Gnome
Wallpaper = Custom

I hope this covers everything.

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-11
> **koleoptero said:**
> What the... does terminator do backgrounds? If it's transparent then It's confused about the part of the screen it's transparent on.
 :P

Basically it's a matter of inserting these into your config

[B]background_type = image
background_image = /home/koleoptero/blah-blah/yadda-yadda/image.jpg[/B]

Or you can just man terminator for more info
... or go here = [http://www.tenshu.net/wp-content/uploads/terminator_config.html](http://www.tenshu.net/wp-content/uploads/terminator_config.html)

Only downside is that, in my isolated case,  xcompmgr sometimes doesn't dropshadow a terminator with an image as background, for some odd reason (as you'll notice in that screenshot)... I probably got something wrong in the config, but can't be arsed to check right now. 

Cheers.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-11
> **gutterslob said:**
> :P

Basically it's a matter of inserting these into your config

[B]background_type = image
background_image = /home/koleoptero/blah-blah/yadda-yadda/image.jpg[/B]

Or you can just man terminator for more info
... or go here = [http://www.tenshu.net/wp-content/uploads/terminator_config.html](http://www.tenshu.net/wp-content/uploads/terminator_config.html)

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-11
@koleoptero
What's wrong with xterm? 

With regards to Terminator, I believe xcompmgr will draw shadows if you comment out all the transparency and opacity related lines in the config and opt for a solid terminal (*[example from an older screenshot]("http://omploader.org/vM2VoMg")*)

Th reason it didn't draw shadows in my previous screenshot is because, as suspected, I forgot to comment out one of the transparency related lines

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-02-11
I'm currently enjoying the Gnome-Shell. I can see the novelty wearing off really, really fast. As far as looks go then I think it does quite well, and changing tasks is only two clicks away so its not radically inefficient. The panel at the top seems mostly wasted and doesn't look all too nice really. Accessing my programs is maybe just a little harder than on the normal desktop, but again its not like I'm wasting heaps of time opening a program. Finding some programs can be slightly harder, e.g. the system monitor, but I guess that's what the search bar is for. 

I think the activities 'button' would be more effective if it was reactive all over, only after a few flukes did I realise it was only the most top left part that was. 

It definitely looks stylish but I fear usability may have been sacrificed.


On a side note, its only once you've gone from Firefox to Google-Chrome, and then back to Firefox that you realise how damn slow Firefox actually is.

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-02-11

### Post by tjwoosta on 2010-02-11
> **walkerk said:**
> This is an annoying development. A year ago (+/-) gnome-terminal/xfce4-terminal and xcompmgr worked well together. I know because I used them. Currently on my system, xcompmgr draws the shadows but the shadows do not move resulting in remnants...

My workaround has been to use xterm though not being able to copy/paste is frustrating.

> you can use middle-click to paste in xterm

Yes, xterm uses the x11 clipboard. Instead of copy and paste in the traditional sense you just highlight something to copy it (no crtl-c or anything, just highlight it) and middle click to paste (if you dont have a middle button just press both buttons together to simulate middle click).

---

### Post by NightwishFan on 2010-02-11
> **Mark76 said:**
> I'm curious to know why the file manager label is partly covering the file manager icon.

It is supposed to do that I guess. It changed in a recent update. (They do change stuff back as well. Also you can now close windows from the overlay (note the "X" over Empathy). There is a new overlay mode that shows one desktop at a time.

Notifications show up at the bottom of the screen. When a track changes, it will show you a small notice. If you mouse over, you can interact. It disappears if you mouse off. In the future I believe notifications will queue.

I have some mockups of how the shell may look in the future. The new startup bar, and the chatback are mockups.

---

### Post by NightwishFan on 2010-02-11
The Gnome Shell is due to be released later this year with Gnome 2.32. Yes, it replaces the Gnome Panel and Nautilus with it's own interface. When the new Gnome is released I believe they will ship the old interface as well. Also, the Gnome Shell uses it's own compositing manager, so it "replaces" compiz if it is run.

If you are running Karmic, you can test the Gnome Shell right from the repository, and then just uninstall it when you are done. If you want a more up to date version, you will have to use the ricotz PPA.

[http://ubuntu-tweak.com/source/ricotz-testing/](http://ubuntu-tweak.com/source/ricotz-testing/)

---

### Post by Kenny_Strawn on 2010-02-11
> **NightwishFan said:**
> The Gnome Shell is due to be released later this year with Gnome 2.32. Yes, it replaces the Gnome Panel and [color="Red"]Nautilus[/color] with it's own interface. When the new Gnome is released I believe they will ship the old interface as well. Also, the Gnome Shell uses it's own compositing manager, so it "replaces" compiz if it is run.

If you are running Karmic, you can test the Gnome Shell right from the repository, and then just uninstall it when you are done. If you want a more up to date version, you will have to use the ricotz PPA.

[http://ubuntu-tweak.com/source/ricotz-testing/](http://ubuntu-tweak.com/source/ricotz-testing/)

Correction: GNOME Panel and [color="Red"]Metacity[/color]. Nautilus will still be there, because it is the file manager - and responsible also for the desktop background and icons. Without it, you will just have a black desktop - and no icons or files. You also wouldn't be able to browse your computer or search for files.

### Post by Islington on 2010-02-11
> **koleoptero said:**
> I just like it. Why is it popular? Well why was elegant-brit popular a couple of years ago? And then shiki? Cause it's good, works well, and is complete (meaning gtk, metacity, full icon theme, emerald theme etc)


Elegant Brit, and shiki both had unique ideas behind them though. Elegant brit was all interesting colorscheme with simple and square gtkwidgets.

Shiki really brought together the titlebar+menubar concept with the inverse dark menus. (also it was not a pixbuf)

I guess I am not seeing what elementary is doing new, because it reminds me of azel theme and arora theme engine.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-12
> **Islington said:**
> Elegant Brit, and shiki both had unique ideas behind them though. Elegant brit was all interesting colorscheme with simple and square gtkwidgets.

Shiki really brought together the titlebar+menubar concept with the inverse dark menus. (also it was not a pixbuf)

I guess I am not seeing what elementary is doing new, because it reminds me of azel theme and arora theme engine.

Well it's not that original, but it does look better than the aforementioned themes, at least in my eyes. Plus it borrows things from the macosx environment like the 1 pixel separator between the sidebar and the icon area of nautilus, and the flat uniform sidebar there. Also the patched version of nautilus with the address bar next to the navigation controls saves space. As for the rest, it's just a trend I believe.

### Post by Megrimn on 2010-02-13
I think I have finally found some zen for my desktop.  I haven't been so happy with it's appearance since never.  Definitely diggin' the orange and blue contrast as well.

It's a cross between a few themes.  I used the window border from [#qDrk](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/%23qDrk?content=117908) and the controls from [Glow in the Darkness](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Glow-in-the-Darkness?content=99907)

The Glow in the Darkness page explains how to get fully transparent panels (save for the random icon or two, I've found).

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-13
> **ctrlmd said:**
> what is the name of the theme 
and how did you make the navigation bar look like that ?
it's nice

The theme is elementary compact, and I'm using the elementary modded nautilus. You can get it from their ppa. Just open a terminal and do:

sudo add-apt-repository ppa:elementaryart/elementarydesktop
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get dist-upgrade

And logout.

---

### Post by ctrlmd on 2010-02-13
> **koleoptero said:**
> The theme is elementary compact, and I'm using the elementary modded nautilus. You can get it from their ppa. Just open a terminal and do:

sudo add-apt-repository ppa:elementaryart/elementarydesktop
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get dist-upgrade

And logout.

Some CSS improvements as well, but remember it's still a pretty crude browser, don't expect it to look even near right. *Extremely* fast and light though (10-20 ram ever) - you can feel the whiplash.  
Buuf, Shiki Dust, and Macchiato as usual for the other parts.

And look, omploader works with it! :D All done through dillo.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-02-14
> **Felliph3 said:**
> Oh cool, Id like to try that, how did you do it? :popcorn:

Copied the main xfce menu in .config/menus/ and edited them, as only to contain certain categories: apps or sys utils/dialogues. Also had to copy a bunch of .desktop files from /usr/share/applications/ to .local/share/applications/, adding individual launchers to newly created top-level categories, so things like gnome-system-monitor would appear in both the top-level of the system menu, as well as the System sub-category in both the system and composite (desktop) menu.

Here's the system menu:
```
<!DOCTYPE Menu PUBLIC "-//freedesktop//DTD Menu 1.0//EN"
  "http://www.freedesktop.org/standards/menu-spec/1.0/menu.dtd">

<Menu>
    <Name>System</Name>
    
    <DefaultAppDirs/>
    <DefaultDirectoryDirs/>
    
    <Include>
        <Category>X-Xfce-Toplevel-System</Category>
    </Include>
    
    <Layout>
	<Merge type="all"/>
	<Separator/>
	<Filename>gnome-system-monitor.desktop</Filename>
	<Filename>xfce4-about-xfce.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-help.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-logout.desktop</Filename>
    </Layout>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>Settings</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-settings.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>Settings</Category>
        </Include>
        
        <Layout>
            <Filename>xfce-settings-manager.desktop</Filename>
            <Separator/>
            <Merge type="all"/>
        </Layout>
        
        <Menu>
            <Name>Screensavers</Name>
            <Directory>xfce-screensavers.directory</Directory>
            <Include>
                <Category>Screensaver</Category>
            </Include>
        </Menu>
    </Menu>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>System</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-system.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>System</Category>
        </Include>
    </Menu>
</Menu>
```

Note the include section near the top. If you want a launcher to appear in the top-level of one menu but not another, change the menu's include category, then edit the launcher's categories to only include one of those categories, not the other.

At the risk of starting a flame war, I cannot fathom why the customisation community for Windows turns out such grotesque creations as that. Styles for Windows either fall on the wrong side of usability, or the wrong side of taste, with the sole notable exception being lassekongo83.

I've often suspected the problem is pixmap theming: it creates too great a temptation for the theme designer to 'go nuts'. Gnome-look.org would also seem to support this thesis, with a myriad of tacky pixmap themes.

Then again, you could always go to the other extreme of OSX, where you can barely tell the difference between the majority of themes.

Metacity: [Milk-Flat-Perfectblue.]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Milk+Flat+PerfectBlue?content=94283")
Icon Theme: working on it. :P
Old Wallpaper is old: I have no idea where I got the original (from one of these threads) but I modded its colours. [Get it here.]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/25s2c0i-abused.jpg")
The dock is AWN from their ppa, with a custom striped background that needs some work.
Panel at the top has globalmenu and music applets.
Conky is lame.

### Post by The Real Dave on 2010-02-16
> **gymophett said:**
> You should try seeding with my crappy speed. I get 4mb/s downloading and only .4mb/s uploading. AGH!
And I'm part of a private torrent tracking site. You have to keep up good ratio to stay there. And it is painful.

You should try it with mine, .44 down and .12 up, the absolute maximum my line will take, and even at that it cuts out a few times a day. That said, I'm not part of a tracking site.

Quite a change from my last one. I think I'm trying to make look my Gnome desktop look more like my Openbox one. Failing of course ;) That said, I think I'll just switch to Openbox on my main computer too. 

Plenty of little details that don't work here, the icons don't quite go with the wallpaper, neither does the conky colour, or the workspace switcher, or the switch user applet. I need a decent set of greyscale icons :( And, even after upgrading to the latest version, Pidgin still insists on creating it's own icon background. 

And to top it all of, the date line in the top conky **refuses** to change it's colour. It just does it's own thing :( 

I'm sick of all these flaws :( I havn't had a Gnome desktop I've loved in ages. It's time to switch to Openbox :)

[[IMG]http://linuxexpresso.files.wordpress.com/2010/02/16-feb-2010.png?w=150&h=120[/IMG]]("http://linuxexpresso.files.wordpress.com/2010/02/16-feb-2010.png")

Here's the conkyrc for that conky too, just in case I'm making some stupid mistake :)

```
# -- Conky settings -- #
background no
update_interval 1
 
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
 
override_utf8_locale yes
 
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes
 
text_buffer_size 2048
imlib_cache_size 0
 
# -- Window specifications -- #
 
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
 
border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0
 
minimum_size 5 50
maximum_width 2000
 
alignment tr
gap_x 10
gap_y 25
 
# -- Graphics settings -- #
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
 
# -- Text settings -- #
use_xft yes
xftfont Bauhaus Md BT:size=15
xftalpha 0.8
 
uppercase no
 
default_color DEDEDE

TEXT
${font Bauhaus Md BT:size=50}${alignr}${time %H.%M}${font}
${voffset -7}${alignr}${time %A, %d %B %Y}
```

Yes, indeed, it was inspired by Diablo II.  The BG came from Diablo III, and I was inspired with the colors to do the rest.  The Orbs do indeed flow with CPU/RAM usage as someone questioned.

So, not a <large> waste of time :D

### Post by Post Monkeh on 2010-02-18
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Copied the main xfce menu in .config/menus/ and edited them, as only to contain certain categories: apps or sys utils/dialogues. Also had to copy a bunch of .desktop files from /usr/share/applications/ to .local/share/applications/, adding individual launchers to newly created top-level categories, so things like gnome-system-monitor would appear in both the top-level of the system menu, as well as the System sub-category in both the system and composite (desktop) menu.

Here's the system menu:
```
<!DOCTYPE Menu PUBLIC "-//freedesktop//DTD Menu 1.0//EN"
  "http://www.freedesktop.org/standards/menu-spec/1.0/menu.dtd">

<Menu>
    <Name>System</Name>
    
    <DefaultAppDirs/>
    <DefaultDirectoryDirs/>
    
    <Include>
        <Category>X-Xfce-Toplevel-System</Category>
    </Include>
    
    <Layout>
	<Merge type="all"/>
	<Separator/>
	<Filename>gnome-system-monitor.desktop</Filename>
	<Filename>xfce4-about-xfce.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-help.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-logout.desktop</Filename>
    </Layout>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>Settings</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-settings.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>Settings</Category>
        </Include>
        
        <Layout>
            <Filename>xfce-settings-manager.desktop</Filename>
            <Separator/>
            <Merge type="all"/>
        </Layout>
        
        <Menu>
            <Name>Screensavers</Name>
            <Directory>xfce-screensavers.directory</Directory>
            <Include>
                <Category>Screensaver</Category>
            </Include>
        </Menu>
    </Menu>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>System</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-system.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>System</Category>
        </Include>
    </Menu>
</Menu>
```

Note the include section near the top. If you want a launcher to appear in the top-level of one menu but not another, change the menu's include category, then edit the launcher's categories to only include one of those categories, not the other.

so that's actually the xfce panel then or is it the goome panel?

you don't explain (either that or i'm missing it) how you are using icons instead of the standard "applications / places / system" menu style.

i'd like to know if there was a way to edit this because my top panel is beginning to get a little cluttered, yet i like having the 3 separate menus

---

### Post by Shhnap on 2010-02-18
I am a programmer that favours efficiency, clean looks and purple themes. As a result I use Gnome for the programs, but instead of using metacity I love xMonad. 

xMonad is a completely awesome tiling window manager and everyone should use it, why waste screen space when you don't have to.

I also use google-chrome for the speed and the awesome themes.

Currently what you see there in image two is google-chrome and two gnome-terminals in three different xMonad tiles. The terminals are running mplayer and alsamixer respectively. I just jammed everything into one so that you could appreciate the tiling effect.

Image one is the screen that I get when I login. I download all of my awesome images from the super cool guys at 3DTotal. As you can see I have the desktop disabled...who needs all of those items cluttering my screen. I like to keep it clean and if I need something I'll just open a terminal and grab it. Or use dwm to open it instead.

And, if you know what you're doing that all takes about 15 min to setup. If you don't, then first time round maybe two hours but it's totally worth it.

Let me know what you think. :D

P.S. I have attached my simple xmonad.hs just in case somebody wants to see it.

---

I would be running Office 2010 beta under wine, but its still broken, so Office 2k7 for now. I also use Dreamweaver and Cool Edit Pro 2.0 under Wine both work flawlessly. ### Post by Gallahhad on 2010-02-19
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Does Dreamweaver CS3 work out good ?

I'm using Dreamweaver 8; I have not bothered upgrading beyond that since it does everything I need, and it's expensive.
[[IMG]http://img62.imageshack.us/img62/9818/dreamweaver8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img62.imageshack.us/i/dreamweaver8.jpg/)
Dreamweaver 8 in wine works perfectly for me, others results may vary, I make no promises. I will say I have done nothing special with wine, I'm using the winehq ppa, and bone stock configuration after that.

The xmonad tiling window manager responded as expected, it most likely requires a bunch of tweaking to get working, I had to remove --purge it to get back to a desktop. I'll continue moving my windows around the way I have for the last 10 years in every operating system I've used; good old mouse drag, and pop through them with alt-tab, and sort by desktops using ctrl-alt-arrow

TWM's have in my opinion never left 1995 in appearance, and they always require a bunch of bs just to get them up and rolling; just not worth it.

### Post by nickylee on 2010-02-19
> **DownTown22 said:**
> Details?

And is that the Now Playing screenlet in the top right corner?  If so, what theme/skin is it?

Okay let's see: AWN 3.9, Now Playing screenlet with [top-right Corner theme]("http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/Corner-4-Nowplaying-127319208?offset=20#comments"), elementary-mod gtk theme as linked above, nautilus-elementary mod, and finally [Cover-thumbnailer]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Cover-thumbnailer?content=120258") Nautilus script.  And as of now, I'm back to using the latest Gnome Shell build as it's now fixed. :D  I've relegated AWN to autohiding and use it for it's applets instead of task switching.

Some notes: As I said above I had to tweak the images in the elementary theme, but I also had to tweak the Now Playing screenlet theme as the one I've linked to is missing a small chunk of corner on the images.  Easily enough fixed and I can share my fix if requested.

### Post by Amtal on 2010-02-19
Upgraded to KDE 4.4. Not everything went smoothly as far as getting my window decorations and plasmoids setup again, but I finally have everything working.

Widget Style: [QtCurve from here]("http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/retroactive-150774364")
Windows: [Aurorae using AirGlass-White]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Airglass-white++%5BAURORAE%5D?content=108392")
Icons: [Kycons]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Kycons?content=115097")
Font: Lucida Grande
Console [Font: Envy Code R]("http://damieng.com/blog/2008/05/26/envy-code-r-preview-7-coding-font-released")
Clock Font: [Geosans Light]("http://www.dafont.com/geo-sans-light.font")
Plasma: [Glassified]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Glassified?content=81388")

### Post by Felliph3 on 2010-02-19
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Copied the main xfce menu in .config/menus/ and edited them, as only to contain certain categories: apps or sys utils/dialogues. Also had to copy a bunch of .desktop files from /usr/share/applications/ to .local/share/applications/, adding individual launchers to newly created top-level categories, so things like gnome-system-monitor would appear in both the top-level of the system menu, as well as the System sub-category in both the system and composite (desktop) menu.

Here's the system menu:
```
<!DOCTYPE Menu PUBLIC "-//freedesktop//DTD Menu 1.0//EN"
  "http://www.freedesktop.org/standards/menu-spec/1.0/menu.dtd">

<Menu>
    <Name>System</Name>
    
    <DefaultAppDirs/>
    <DefaultDirectoryDirs/>
    
    <Include>
        <Category>X-Xfce-Toplevel-System</Category>
    </Include>
    
    <Layout>
	<Merge type="all"/>
	<Separator/>
	<Filename>gnome-system-monitor.desktop</Filename>
	<Filename>xfce4-about-xfce.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-help.desktop</Filename>
        <Filename>xfce4-logout.desktop</Filename>
    </Layout>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>Settings</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-settings.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>Settings</Category>
        </Include>
        
        <Layout>
            <Filename>xfce-settings-manager.desktop</Filename>
            <Separator/>
            <Merge type="all"/>
        </Layout>
        
        <Menu>
            <Name>Screensavers</Name>
            <Directory>xfce-screensavers.directory</Directory>
            <Include>
                <Category>Screensaver</Category>
            </Include>
        </Menu>
    </Menu>
    
    <Menu>
        <Name>System</Name>
        <Directory>xfce-system.directory</Directory>
        <Include>
            <Category>System</Category>
        </Include>
    </Menu>
</Menu>
```

Note the include section near the top. If you want a launcher to appear in the top-level of one menu but not another, change the menu's include category, then edit the launcher's categories to only include one of those categories, not the other.


Cool thanks!

---

### Post by tjwoosta on 2010-02-20
Tiling wm's really work best if your a cli type of person (or at least a keyboard person). When set up right you never even have to touch the mouse. 

Window management becomes instantaneous with just the press of a key. No moving windows around and resizing them all the time, just bam and your on another workspace using a different app.

I tried to save as much screen space as possible for this. Please don't take this as a mac inspired setup - the similarities with the OSX interface are all coincidences. The fact is that in recent times, I have hated few things as much as apple's stance on certain issues, and it would pain me to be assosciated with those bastards. I want ubuntu to be different too, and there* are* a few significant differences here...
I know what you mean about being ticked off at Apple. There are times I wish I had an OSX-like theme that wouldn't actually be an OSX-looking theme for that very reason, but I keep coming back to the Mac4Lin theme. Perhaps one day I'll find a nice theme that combines Elementary's color scheme, Mac4Lin's icons, and enough differences from the (snow) leopard that I'll finally have a theme I can call my own. The new default Lucid theme may just do the trick depending on how it ends up looking.

### Post by ctrlmd on 2010-02-22

:ois there something like that in gnome with flag thx

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-22
> **ctrlmd said:**
> :ois there something like that in gnome with flag thx

Unfortunately no. While XFCE might not be as popular as Gnome, some things are much better in it. The panel is one of those. It has by default a lot of applets available that in gnome you have to work to get them working. The keyboard indicator applet has the option to switch between showing the flags or just the text in xfce, while in gnome there are no such options. In gnome you must go to some trouble to install dockbarx while xfce has the icon box applet installed by default. And (one reason I absolutely hate gnome-panel) the notification area has the option to hide some of the icons and click an arrow to show them when needed in xfce while in gnome you have to see the whole ugliness of them (openoffice quickstarter, dropbox, etc...).

Sorry for the long responce. LOL

---

well, in gnome (and any DE) you can make some progs have no tray icon by adding -notrayicon to the command. 

anyway, your argument is a bit odd, since - while you may have to put some effort initially, once those 5 minutes of effort are done, it's done, and that's it. 5 minutes of effort are not a good argument to defend a DE or attack another.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-02-22
> **TheNessus said:**
> well, in gnome (and any DE) you can make some progs have no tray icon by adding -notrayicon to the command. 

anyway, your argument is a bit odd, since - while you may have to put some effort initially, once those 5 minutes of effort are done, it's done, and that's it. 5 minutes of effort are not a good argument to defend a DE or attack another.

First of all having no tray icon is very different from having a hidden tray icon. I want the icon there, just hidden. I click on the arrow and, poof, icon's there. Want to get on the dropbox website click the arrow, click the dropbox icon and you're there. It's different.

Secondly, I am expressing an opinion about said DE's. I'm not attacking nor defending anything. I was not looking to provoke an argument. I've been a Gnome user for a looong time, and I would not even say that I won't switch to Gnome again in the future.

XFCE is missing stuff too, like a tool to edit the colours of the gtk theme as easily as in gnome. What I am trying to say though, is that Gnome has sacrificed a lot of options on the altar of ease of use. And with the popularity that Gnome has (which I'm not saying if it's worth it or not) one would expect some features to be already implemented or added to the defaults.

And those "5 minutes of effort" are more than 5 to the inexperienced user, and overall time better spent doing anything else.

KDE and XFCE offer many options and a lot of functionality that gnome doesn't by having such small stuff in their system. That's why I use xfce now. If I wanted something Gnome offered but XFCE didn't then I would be using gnome, as I imagine many people do.

---

never used XFCE though.

### Post by proxess on 2010-02-23
> **armageddon08 said:**
> How'd you make your firefox look like that?

Giant Speck used an integrated all in one menu plugin, moved the bookmarks to the menu bar and the icons with a flexible spacer between the bookmarks and the icons, then the icons display only text, removed the search bar and the activity indicator, and kept the address bar.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-02-24
Speaking of being all edgy and geeky and what-have-you, I just made Totem usable. With some srsly hardc0re XML editing (after realising the hard way that Glade 2/3 breaks Totem) of /usr/share/totem/totem.ui, I managed to get rid of that stupid border around the video box and gave Totem's controls a more compact layout.

[img]http://img710.imageshack.us/img710/1779/totemb.jpg[/img]

This is good, as I now need totem, since it seems to be the only video programme capable of playing back videos in a way that doesn't screw with my TV's 100hz judder reduction.

### Post by hhh on 2010-02-24
@gutterslob, that's going to look awesome when you finish matching the menu colors.

@koleoptero, I'm in love with Terminator. Problem solved, and thank you!

@mcduck,

I rarely use multiple workspaces, so I hadn't run into your bug. It's caused by a conflict with Gnome Display Manager...
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/openbox/+bug/435638](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/openbox/+bug/435638)

So making this the first line of my autostart.sh WFM...
```
xprop -root -remove _NET_NUMBER_OF_DESKTOPS -remove _NET_DESKTOP_NAMES -remove _NET_CURRENT_DESKTOP &
```

I stopped drawing shadows under my panel, but try this at the end of autostart.sh
```

(sleep 2 && tint2) &
(sleep 3 && xcompmgr -cfF -I-.002 -O-.003 -t-5 -l-5 -r4.2 -o.55 -D1) &
```

HTH

Here's my rarely used Gnome session in action. Wall is from the gnome-backgrounds package, Emerald theme is showtime, GTK+ is Clearlooks Classic, icons are airlines, and the music player is the awesome but horribly named Last.fm client Vagalume...

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM25pcw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM25pcw)

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM25pdA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM25pdA)

> @mcduck,

I rarely use multiple workspaces, so I hadn't run into your bug. It's caused by a conflict with Gnome Display Manager...
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/openbox/+bug/435638](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/openbox/+bug/435638)

So making this the first line of my autostart.sh WFM...
```
xprop -root -remove _NET_NUMBER_OF_DESKTOPS -remove _NET_DESKTOP_NAMES -remove _NET_CURRENT_DESKTOP &
```

I stopped drawing shadows under my panel, but try this at the end of autostart.sh
```

```

thanks for that, I actually got the Tint shadows working  (I already had 3 second delay for xcompmgr, changed that to 5 seconds which seems to be enough. Not for Gnome-terminal, though, but I'm not going  to add any more delay just because of that.

But at least I now have the correct amount of workspaces, that problem was more than annoying. :D

I couldn't stand a desktop without enough workspaces, I've had four for almost as long as I've used a graphical desktop and at some point the very idea of having to manage all the windows on only one workspace starts to feel impossible..

btw, no screenshot. My desktop is still the same it was half a year ago, I haven't found any theme or wallpaper that I'd actually like better than what I already use and every time I do something with Conky or other stuff I end removing it from my desktop after a day or two. I think I just have realized that my computer works just fine without me monitoring what it's doing, all I need is a clock and something to show me my minimized windows. ;)

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-26
> **Diptansu said:**
> Thanks nephish .. I just closed the default system tray .. and now its working with tint2 :) .. Thanks again ..

But still I cant get panel I hv seen in some screenshots here. Can I put some Icons in there too, like some dock? some ppl seems to have more than one taskbar in that panel !! .. err ..
You still haven't mentioned what environment you're using (Gnome, Xfce, Openbox?)

For multiple desktops to show, you just add the line **taskbar_mode = multi_desktop** 

If you want only task icons to show, make sure **task_icon = 1 **and **task_text = 0**

If you need more help, you should post your current tint2rc and a screenshot to make it easier for people to assist you.

Hope this helps.
Cheers

```
# Tint2 config file
# Generated by tintwizard (http://code.google.com/p/tintwizard/)

# For information on manually configuring tint2 see http://code.google.com/p/tint2/wiki/Configure

# To use this as default tint2 config: save as $HOME/.config/tint2/tint2rc

# Background definitions
# ID 1
rounded = 5
border_width = 1
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #0D0404 100

# Panel
panel_monitor = all

panel_size = 1460 24
panel_margin = -200 0
panel_padding = 10 0
panel_dock = 0
wm_menu = 0
panel_background_id = 0

# Taskbar
taskbar_mode = single_desktop
taskbar_padding = 200 0 5
taskbar_background_id = 0
taskbar_active_background_id = 0

# Tasks
urgent_nb_of_blink = 7
task_icon = 1
task_text = 1
task_centered = 1
task_maximum_size = 200 32
task_padding = 20 5
task_background_id = 1
task_active_background_id = 1
task_icon_asb = 0 0 0
task_active_icon_asb = 0 0 0

# Fonts
task_font = Sans 9
task_font_color = #F9F4F4 100
task_active_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
font_shadow = 0

# Systray
systray_padding = 0 0 0
systray_sort = right2left
systray_background_id = 0

# Clock
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = Sans 10
clock_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
clock_padding = 10 0
clock_background_id = 1

# Tooltips
tooltip = 1
tooltip_padding = 0 0
tooltip_show_timeout = 0
tooltip_hide_timeout = 0
tooltip_background_id = 0
tooltip_font = San 12
tooltip_font_color = #FFFFFF 100

# Mouse
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = none
mouse_scroll_down = none

# Battery
battery = 1
battery_low_status = 20
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
bat1_font = San 12
bat2_font = San 12
battery_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
battery_padding = 0 0
battery_background_id = 0

# End of config
```

Thanks in advance ..

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-02-26
@Diptansu
Looking at your config, I'd suggest you use more than one background ID (most people have 3) ... that way, you can have your panel_background_id =1 and systray_background_id=1 , your task_active_background_id=2 and something else=3, for example.
I'd paste my tintrc for you, but mine is much too different from what you're aiming at.
Why not go here = [http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/3232/my-tint2-config/](http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/3232/my-tint2-config/) and grab a config that is closest to what you're looking for, and then modify it to suit your style.

### Post by hhh on 2010-02-26
> **Diptansu said:**
> Secondly, if I unclick 'expand' in a gnome panel, I found two white bars at the ends which are not transparent. Is there anything can be done to make them transparent as well?
No. You can color them though, which will make them look transparent if you use a solid-colored background...

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM283MA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM283MA)

To do that, create a hidden file in your /home/USER_NAME folder named .gtkrc-2.0 (if you don't have one already) and add this to it...

```
#custom panel colors in gnome
style "panel"
{
    bg[NORMAL]               = "#587C8F"
    fg[NORMAL]               = "#C9D5DB"
}
widget "*PanelWidget*" style "panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget_class "*Mail*" style "panel"
class "*notif*" style "panel"
class "*Notif*" style "panel"
class "*Tray*" style "panel"
class "*tray*" style "panel"
```

The "bg[NORMAL] =" number is a color hex code for the panel bars (or the whole panel if you haven't set it to "transparent") which you can find by right-clicking your Gnome desktop, choose "Change Desktop Background>Background>Colors, then click the color box and then the eyedropper icon, then click anywhere on your desktop and that color code will show in the "Color Name" box. The "fg[normal]" code will set you panel text color (#000000 is black, #ffffff is white). HTH.

---

### Post by Diptansu on 2010-02-26
> **hhh said:**
> No. You can color them though, which will make them look transparent if you use a solid-colored background...

[[img]http://omploader.org/tM283MA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vM283MA)

To do that, create a hidden file in your /home/USER_NAME folder named .gtkrc-2.0 (if you don't have one already) and add this to it...

```
#custom panel colors in gnome
style "panel"
{
    bg[NORMAL]               = "#587C8F"
    fg[NORMAL]               = "#C9D5DB"
}
widget "*PanelWidget*" style "panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget_class "*Mail*" style "panel"
class "*notif*" style "panel"
class "*Notif*" style "panel"
class "*Tray*" style "panel"
class "*tray*" style "panel"
```

The "bg[NORMAL] =" number is a color hex code for the panel bars (or the whole panel if you haven't set it to "transparent") which you can find by right-clicking your Gnome desktop, choose "Change Desktop Background>Background>Colors, then click the color box and then the eyedropper icon, then click anywhere on your desktop and that color code will show in the "Color Name" box. The "fg[normal]" code will set you panel text color (#000000 is black, #ffffff is white). HTH.

Dont know why it didnt work with me .. :(

What I did is ..

* Found that I do not have a file named .gtkrc-2.0 in /home/USER_NAME
* Open text editor, Copy Pasted your code, Saved it in /home/USER_NAME
* Got the color code and changed bg[NORMAL]

Still there is no change.

Have I done something stupid? If two panel is active which one wd it change? Or will change all the panels?

### Post by GSF1200S on 2010-02-27
> **matty-guy said:**
> The speed of chrome makes up for the one extra time you'll have to scroll your mouse ..

In stock form you are definitely correct. However, load the cache into a temporary filesystem in RAM, enable pipelining, do the ng.display tick in about:config, disable the paint delays, and firefox becomes a little faster than chrome (most of the time, depends on Java content).

Granted, chrome doesnt need these hacks and im sure you can hack chrome to make it even faster. Just thought id mention this so everyone isnt under the impression that firefox is still a dog.
